          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_6283934').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_6283934').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_6283934').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script></div>

<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's fine. It was actually his first published novel, and the two that predate it in terms of the timeline were therefore published afterwards. I just<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's fine. It was actually his first published novel, and the two that predate it in terms of the timeline were therefore published afterwards. I just finished it myself, with it being the first I read. No problem.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_343375183">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343375183" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4988481-peter-meredith" class="left imgcol" title="Peter Meredith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442460979p2/4988481.jpg" alt="Peter Meredith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/343375183?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4988481-peter-meredith" class="user" title="Peter Meredith">Peter Meredith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer343375183">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6846005310557962365">After reading Fifty Shades of Girl Smut, I think I need a manly book. The Hunt for Red October seems virile enough. Strong sweaty men...at sea...with not a woman in sight. Wait a sec! What am I getting in to? They better not start singing, "In the Navy" or "Y.M.C.A." And if there's even a single fashion tip, I'm tossing this book!<br />Wow, what a wonderful book. This is number two on my Clancy book list, right behind Red Storm Rising.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_22790379">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22790379" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1174786-lance" class="left imgcol" title="Lance"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296857692p2/1174786.jpg" alt="Lance" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/22790379?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1174786-lance" class="user" title="Lance">Lance</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1124906.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425083833" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22790379">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12494472546219512580">I read this when I was on the USS Eisenhower. It was so popular with the Squids that I think it replaced the BMR. The thing that really impressed everyone on the ship was how accurate Clancy was with both his research and his story-telling. There was never a "that's not how it happens" moment, so common in media of this type. Engaging story, meticulous research combine for a fantastic read. I recommend this one to everyone.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer446508058">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2136495437465375404">At the tail end of the Cold War, Captain Marko Ramius of the Soviet Navy,decides to defect. Incredibly planning to bring the most advanced submarine in the world with him.The Red October has a new drive system that is virtually noiseless.The nuclear vessel would be almost undetectable. A great advantage against the U.S. and its Allies.But the charismatic Ramius is a bitter man.The widower,and half Lithuanian blames the Soviet Union, for the botched operation that killed his beloved wife.He has r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2136495437465375404">At the tail end of the Cold War, Captain Marko Ramius of the Soviet Navy,decides to defect. Incredibly planning to bring the most advanced submarine in the world with him.The Red October has a new drive system that is virtually noiseless.The nuclear vessel would be almost undetectable. A great advantage against the U.S. and its Allies.But the charismatic Ramius is a bitter man.The widower,and half Lithuanian blames the Soviet Union, for the botched operation that killed his beloved wife.He has recruited unmarried and loyal officers to follow his orders.Telling the rest of the crew that they're going on a friendship visit to Cuba!Leaving from a frozen Arctic port in early December,he needs an icebreaker to get to the open gray sea.The captain looking back at the coast with a touch of melancholy,for the last time.The chilly wind makes everyone outside uncomfortable.From northern Russia,The Red October, heads west to the American dominated Atlantic Ocean. Underwater the giant boat travels slowly.115 crewmen and 15 officers are soon hunted by the Soviets.Ships from above and below the seas and planes from the skies, all want to capture or destroy the renegade sub.The KGB man aboard has to be neutralized.But are there others?Back at the C.I.A. headquarters in the suburbs of Washington, Jack Ryan receives information ,clandestine pictures of the new Soviet submarine.The puzzling photos baffle the uneasy experts.A dangerous development in the balance of power, between the two superpowers...And the northern Soviet Fleet is on the high seas, on course to reach the eastern coast of the United States,very soon.A military exercise or War? The President has a mission for the spy agency's analyst.Become a secret agent.Ryan is not happy.Exciting cat and mouse scenes amongst Soviet, American and British airplanes,ships and submarines.The final underwater battle is a particularly great page- turner.If you get seasick reading Moby Dick,not recommended for you.....</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2136495437465375404">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of political thrillers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer218807067">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11910042701698435212">Yes, I may be fashionably late to this party, considering the threat of war between Soviet Russia -- which doesn't exist anymore -- and Imperialist America is a major theme of this novel. <br /><br />But I figured this should be my first experience with Tom Clancy, and I do not regret my decision at all. This is a near-perfect political thriller, juggling a dozen major characters on two continents as well as a myriad number of ships -- both on and under the Atlantic Ocean. While it was a bit tricky keeping</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11910042701698435212">Yes, I may be fashionably late to this party, considering the threat of war between Soviet Russia -- which doesn't exist anymore -- and Imperialist America is a major theme of this novel. <br /><br />But I figured this should be my first experience with Tom Clancy, and I do not regret my decision at all. This is a near-perfect political thriller, juggling a dozen major characters on two continents as well as a myriad number of ships -- both on and under the Atlantic Ocean. While it was a bit tricky keeping track of everything at a few points, the minor confusion was well worth the scope of what Clancy achieved.<br /><br />I also loved how I was fooled into thinking a later plot event was a rather weak climax, only to not have yet reached the true climax, which does not disappoint at all <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Underwater submarine torpedo battle! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />As a side note, when they wanted to make a movie out of this board game: <img width="400" height="200" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360567i/711489.jpg" /><br />All they had to do was adapt this book again, instead of doing this: <img width="400" height="200" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398715147i/9454639.jpg" /><br />But I guess that would have been too easy. Sigh.<br /><br />Update: Okay, maybe I spoke too soon about the theme of this book being outdated. What a difference a year makes.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_852592875">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852592875" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="left imgcol" title="Rob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" alt="Rob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/852592875?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="user" title="Rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/18667347-the-hunt-for-red-october" title="Audiobook " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book" class="actionLinkLite">audio-book</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=jack-ryan" class="actionLinkLite">jack-ryan</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=stand-alone" class="actionLinkLite">stand-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer852592875">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2923035968193553103"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> A pretty fun spy thriller that occasionally gets bogged down by too much military jargon.<br /><br /><strong>Audio book:</strong> This is my first time listening to a book read by J. Charles. He's a pretty good reader. I initially felt like he read too fast, but I either got used to it, or he slowed down. He does many accents, although with multiple Russian characters, I'm not sure if he made them all sound the same, or I simply couldn't tell them apart.<br /><br />The book also uses sound effects to simulate phone c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2923035968193553103"><strong>Executive Summary:</strong> A pretty fun spy thriller that occasionally gets bogged down by too much military jargon.<br /><br /><strong>Audio book:</strong> This is my first time listening to a book read by J. Charles. He's a pretty good reader. I initially felt like he read too fast, but I either got used to it, or he slowed down. He does many accents, although with multiple Russian characters, I'm not sure if he made them all sound the same, or I simply couldn't tell them apart.<br /><br />The book also uses sound effects to simulate phone calls and radio talk on the ships/submarines that I thought was well done. All and all I think the audiobook edition adds something extra to the story.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</strong><br />This is my first time reading this book. I had previously seen and enjoyed the movie. It's been awhile so I have a hard time comparing the two. I might have slightly enjoyed the movie more however.<br /><br />There are a few parts of this book that seemed to get bogged down with too much military jargon and side antidotes that I don't think always added much to the main story.<br /><br />The main story however is a lot of fun though. There is a reason why several of Mr. Clancy's Jack Ryan books have been turned into movies. He does a great job writing a fast pace spy novel that translates well to a big screen. It doesn't seem like they had to do too much to the story to make a good movie out of it.<br /><br />This isn't a book for great character depth or intricate subplots, but was the perfect choice as a palette cleanser from the last book I listened to. Most people are probably familiar with Tom Clancy and most likely Jack Ryan. He's not really a gun-toting action hero, but an intelligent analyst able to out think his enemies.<br /><br />I plan to continue on in the series (in publication order rather than chronological order) at some point, especially if I can get a hold of them in audiobook for cheap or from the library.<br /><br />3.5 Stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2923035968193553103">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_39958691">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39958691" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1690477-hunter" class="left imgcol" title="Hunter"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Hunter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/39958691?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 12, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1690477-hunter" class="user" title="Hunter">Hunter</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39958691">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4660562146696007038">The Hunt for Red October by Tom Clancy<br />Tom Clancy explains just how dangerous it must be to work on a submarine. The better half of this story takes place in the Atlantic Ocean somewhere between North America and Europe, in the 1980s. CIA agent, Jack Ryan finds out just how hard it is to find a submarine that appears to fool even the best sonar men.<br /><br />Jack Ryan is one of the main characters that I liked in this story. He is a persistent human being in that he is unwilling to give up without capturin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4660562146696007038">The Hunt for Red October by Tom Clancy<br />Tom Clancy explains just how dangerous it must be to work on a submarine. The better half of this story takes place in the Atlantic Ocean somewhere between North America and Europe, in the 1980s. CIA agent, Jack Ryan finds out just how hard it is to find a submarine that appears to fool even the best sonar men.<br /><br />Jack Ryan is one of the main characters that I liked in this story. He is a persistent human being in that he is unwilling to give up without capturing the Red October. He is the main reason I liked the book. He is a very interesting character because he is extremely motivated to find the Red October and is always taking action, which often leads to conflict. <br /><br />Marco Ramius is the captain of the elusive Red October. He wishes to defect because he feels that the United States of America holds more for him than Russia ever will. Since Marco Ramius’ wife died the preceding year, he has no family left in Russia so therefore he has nothing to lose by defecting. In Russia, Ramius had never experienced freedom, which is another reason he wishes to become a United States citizen. <br /><br />Jack Ryan trails Marco Ramius for countless miles. Skip Tyler, an expert when it comes to submarines and a good friend of Jack Ryan, helps the CIA find out what they are up against when they receive pictures of a new Typhoon class Russian Submarine. Skip Tyler is able to figure out what makes this new submarine so silent. Almost the whole time during the story, the Red October is being closely pursued or attacked.<br /><br />The Hunt for Red October takes place in the 1980s, nearly 30 years ago, but the writer makes it seem so real that the reader feels as if the story is happening in the present day.<br />The main theme of this book is that teamwork is important. Marco Ramius and Jack Ryan later find out that by working together, more can be accomplished than working by themselves. <br /><br />This whole story is based around the simple want for freedom, the desire to live and do as you please. Freedom is something that should be given to everyone. Will Marco Ramius achieve his freedom by coming to America? Will he be destroyed by his enemies, or maybe even his own allies? If you want to find the answer to these questions, you will have to read the book.<br /><br /><br /><br />Page Count: 469<br />Genre: Espionage<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4660562146696007038">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_287261962">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287261962" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="left imgcol" title="Jane Stewart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" alt="Jane Stewart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/287261962?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="user" title="Jane Stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7978202-the-hunt-for-red-october" title="MP3 CD 9781441850553" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=military-historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">military-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer287261962">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5488333139011018853">Writer’s style is not engaging or entertaining for me. He’s probably good for military technical buffs.<br /><br />This guy is a popular best selling author. But not for me. I assume his fans are those who love to think and talk about military technical stuff - with a story to go along with it. The author is regularly welcomed aboard jets, submarines, and destroyers. Admirals and generals give him access, Pentagon officials debrief him, and many of his books are required reading at military colleges. So I a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5488333139011018853">Writer’s style is not engaging or entertaining for me. He’s probably good for military technical buffs.<br /><br />This guy is a popular best selling author. But not for me. I assume his fans are those who love to think and talk about military technical stuff - with a story to go along with it. The author is regularly welcomed aboard jets, submarines, and destroyers. Admirals and generals give him access, Pentagon officials debrief him, and many of his books are required reading at military colleges. So I assume he is accurate about these things.<br /><br />MY PROBLEMS:<br />There were too many characters to keep track of. And for each character, I only knew them through their work. There was no emotional development of characters, no seeing their feelings. I felt like this was “bring your daughter to work day,” and I was going along with my dad (and many other dads) listening and watching as they did their work and attended meetings. I wasn’t excited about anything. Parts were boring. I listened to the sonar guy for a while, then I listened to the captain of a ship for a while, then I listened to the Russian leaders meet and talk about what to do, then I listened to the CIA meet and talk about what to do, then a guy calls another guy talking about what to do. Throughout the book the reader is jumping around among different groups of military and political people.<br /><br />I want interesting characters to watch, characters that pull me in emotionally. I want witty, interesting, or enlightening dialogue. I want interesting events that move the plot along. There were two interesting major climactic resolutions, but it took way too long to get to them, with nothing else good along the way. It was just watch the guys work. My mind wandered too often, and I wished it would be over.<br /><br />I saw the movie many years ago and loved it. The movie had a very different feel, and it ended sooner than the book. I think the movie was one of those “inspired by” movies rather than “based on” the book. In the BOOK Jack and other U.S. leaders all believe Marco (the captain of the RO) wants to defect, and they have a plan and prepare for it. In the MOVIE, Jack believes Marco wants to defect but another US commander doesn’t. The commander plans to blow up the RO, and Jack has to convince him not to. At one point Jack lies to the US commander saying I know Marco so well that I know he will turn left at the next something. Jack was bluffing. But when Marco coincidentally turned left, the US commander cancels the order to attack. That scene was so intense that I still remember it all these years later. Nothing like that was in the book.<br /><br />Anyway I wanted to try Tom Clancy, which is why I read this, but I won’t be reading any more.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />The book is set around 1983, during the days of the “Cold War” between the U.S. and the USSR. It illustrates some of the thinking back then with nuclear threats on both sides. This is one of many books in the Jack Ryan series. Jack is an analyst for the CIA. The Red October is the name of a Russian submarine. The captain of the RO does not follow orders and is on the run from other USSR subs and ships. Jack is the first one to suggest the captain might want to defect. The U.S. navy and the Russian fleet are all trying to find the RO.<br /><br />NARRATOR:<br />The narrator J. Charles spoke too quickly. It was jarring to concentrate on his speed of talking. Even between scenes and chapters there were almost no pauses.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook reading time: 16 hrs and 47 mins. Swearing language: strong, including religious swear words. Sexual content: none. Setting: Around 1983 U.S., USSR (Russia), and the Atlantic Ocean. Book copyright: 1984. Genre: military historical fiction. Ending: happy for the good guys.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5488333139011018853">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/40533928?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="user" title="Manny">Manny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40533928">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13838727320350334131">Everyone always goes on about how meticulous Tom Clancy's background research is, but there was a moment in this book which made me wonder. They're going to run a big program on a military computer, and (being gamblin' military men) they decide to bet on how long it will take to complete. One of them asks how long the program is - number of lines, or punched cards, or whatever. The other one tells him, and then the first guy makes his estimate.<br /><br />I'm sorry, this no doubt shows what a mean-spirited</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13838727320350334131">Everyone always goes on about how meticulous Tom Clancy's background research is, but there was a moment in this book which made me wonder. They're going to run a big program on a military computer, and (being gamblin' military men) they decide to bet on how long it will take to complete. One of them asks how long the program is - number of lines, or punched cards, or whatever. The other one tells him, and then the first guy makes his estimate.<br /><br />I'm sorry, this no doubt shows what a mean-spirited person I am, but it did cross my mind to wonder if Mr. Clancy knew what a loop was. I'm ashamed of myself. I'm sure there's any number of perfectly reasonable explanations.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13838727320350334131">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_445120309">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445120309" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/14107402-paul-didham" class="left imgcol" title="Paul Didham"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Paul Didham" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/445120309?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14107402-paul-didham" class="user" title="Paul Didham">Paul Didham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer445120309">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6723174269211780997"> The Hunt for Red October <br /><br /><br />The Hunt for Red October is a thrill ride you won't want to miss from start to finish the plot keeps you guessing. Why is he doing this? What is his motive? Tom Clancy's unique writing style ties everything together. From engaging characters to an intriguing plot for me it was a must read.<br /><br /> The year is 1984, A russian nuclear submarine is steaming to the united states the Americans what her the russians want her back. Could this mean war or is it trying to defect? The Re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6723174269211780997">	The Hunt for Red October <br /><br /><br />The Hunt for Red October is a thrill ride you won't want to miss from start to finish the plot keeps you guessing. Why is he doing this? What is his motive? Tom Clancy's unique writing style ties everything together. From engaging characters to an intriguing plot for me it was a must read.<br /><br />	The year is 1984, A russian nuclear submarine is steaming to the united states the Americans what her the russians want her back. Could this mean war or is it trying to defect? The Red October was the pride of the soviet navy, designed and commanded by Marko Ramius a captain of the first rank. A trusted party member who has gone rogue and is trying to defect to the United States of America but, Its more complicated than it seems. Ramius father was a hero of the revolution but, to Ramius his father was hardly a hero. For Ramius the state had robbed him of his father that was not the only thing the state would rob him of. On the other side of the iron gate lies CIA analyst Jack Ryan a modest man who speaks his mind. By determination, luck and skill he rose through the ranks of the CIA and now is one of their most trusted analyst. He has the knowledge and the willpower to get the job done. <br /><br />	Marko Ramius once a proud loyal soviet who would do anything for the cause. A son of a party chieftain his father was a hero of the revolution but, Ramius had little in common with his father. One thing he learned as a young man was that the state had been corrupted, his old mentor the man that taught him about submarines a good man had died because he had no place to live. Later on his wife would die because, the state had inadequate doctor with poor training. Also Ramius would learn there was nothing he could do. This lead to hate and over time his hate manifested itself into an idea then a plain. A last revenge on the state that had taken so much from him and giving so little yes for Marko Ramius it was the only way. <br /><br />	Tom clancy does a great job at making Marko Ramius a likable believable character. This man motivated by revenge trying to escape from tyranny to freedom. Has plenty of obstacles to overcome on his journey, that shows exactly what kind of person he is. You see this near the end of the book when its all over Ramius is empty not happy not sad. He had his revenge but in the end it didn't make him happier.<br /><br />	The Hunt for Red October is a perfect example of what was going on during the cold war. People were defecting, also this shows how corrupt communism was. How it favored the few and enslaved the masses. Tom Clancy showed this point in a easy to grasp way through an exciting novel. Still the underlying theme that was shown in the book is revenge doesn't pay, after all Marko Ramius did he felt empty after it was all done.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6723174269211780997">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_779797794">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779797794" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/25128322-eric-jonrosh" class="left imgcol" title="Eric Jonrosh"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Eric Jonrosh" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/779797794?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25128322-eric-jonrosh" class="user" title="Eric Jonrosh">Eric Jonrosh</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer779797794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5146077414559729380">What's more Russian than a Scotsman?<br /><br />I first discovered “The Hunt for Red October” when the late, great Tom Clancy, informed me that the source material would be converted to film in the summer of ’89. When he explained that none other than Sir Sean Connery would play a crucial part, I immediately grew red in the face and hurled my glass of scotch into the fire quite dramatically. Regretting that impulsive act, I poured myself another glass, much larger than the first. When Tom inquired why I rea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5146077414559729380">What's more Russian than a Scotsman?<br /><br />I first discovered “The Hunt for Red October” when the late, great Tom Clancy, informed me that the source material would be converted to film in the summer of ’89. When he explained that none other than Sir Sean Connery would play a crucial part, I immediately grew red in the face and hurled my glass of scotch into the fire quite dramatically. Regretting that impulsive act, I poured myself another glass, much larger than the first. When Tom inquired why I reacted so violently, I hurled that glass into the fire as well. Sit back, dear readers, and prepare to be aroused and astounded.<br /><br />When I first met my ancient nemesis Sean Connery, we were working together on a film called “The Highlander.” I was of a particular help because I’d written a poem in 1965 about a Scottish man trapped in the body of a Portuguese sailor. It won no great accolades, mostly because one couldn’t read it without weeping uncontrollably. <br /><br />After we wrapped each night on the Isle of Skye, Christopher Lambert, Sean and myself would go down to a local public house called The Sheep’s Shaft and drink scotch, sometimes for days at a time. It was disastrous for the production, but a proper scotch diet tends to break a few eggs. Then one fateful night, Sir Connery became my eternal nemesis forever. I couldn’t say what happened for certain, but I awoke the next morn, fully clothed at the rail station with a frightening message scrawled on the palm of my hand:<br /><br />“Show your leathery face on the moors of Scotland again, Eric Jonrosh, and I’ll cask your headless corpse in a Scotch barrel. Warmest Regards, Sean Connery”<br /><br />As delicious as that might sound, I took heed of the threat and never returned to that peaty bog of a country. Now I am forced to buy my scotch by the can.<br /><br />So it stands to reason that Mr. Connery would make a perfect Russian turncoat submarine captain. And I daresay he nailed the performance in “The Hunt for Red October.” I imagine he just played himself. Likely because he couldn’t conjure a Russian accent to save his malty skin. He would have made a fine Winston Morehouse in my retelling of the heartbreaking epic “The Spoils of Babylon,” airing on IFC this very January the 9th, 2014. Alas, Mr. Connery is approximately 900 hundred years old, so, I cast the uber-talented Marty Comanche instead. He too is now my eternal nemesis.<br /><br />Warmest Regards,<br /><br />Eric Jonrosh, spellbinding creator of “The Spoils of Babylon,” airing on IFC, January the 9th, 2014<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5146077414559729380">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3907643617318465571">I read all but a couple of Clancy's Ryan/Clark books and find them good in the extreme.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText3907643617318465571">I read all but a couple of Clancy's Ryan/Clark books and find them good in the extreme. I do prefer Vince Flynn and Brad Thor, but they're somewhat different (well their characters are closer to Clark than Ryan). In this one Ryan still hasn't actually started his political career... But he does get drawn into the danger, again.<br /><br />Jack (an annalist for the CIA)manages to get tagged to fly photos to the UK...from there he ends trying to convince the powers in charge that a Russian sub captain is trying to defect, not get close enough to the US (with the revolutionary new quiet drive Soviet sub) to launch an attack on the country. High level attitude? Sink the sub... Jack needs to convince everyone otherwise.<br /><br />Thumbnail synopsis but...if you've managed to get by till now without seeing the movie and you're thinking of reading the book I don't want to ruin it for you.<br /><br />Enjoy. </span>

        <a href="/review/show/71586261?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2723599-chad-sayban" class="user" title="Chad Sayban">Chad Sayban</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1001555.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Hardcover 9780870212857" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=highly-recommended" class="actionLinkLite">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=home-library" class="actionLinkLite">home-library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer71586261">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14167720354774442345">I was 12 years old, living at the height of the Cold War in 1984 and <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> hit me like a lightning bolt. I hadn’t read anything like it – in fact, nobody had. What can you say about a book and an author who single-handedly invented a genre – the techno-thriller – and became one of the bestselling authors of the 1990s? The Hunt for Red October has it all – fast pacing, great characters, a highly inventive plot that was so realistic it had people wondering if Clancy was privy to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14167720354774442345">I was 12 years old, living at the height of the Cold War in 1984 and <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> hit me like a lightning bolt. I hadn’t read anything like it – in fact, nobody had. What can you say about a book and an author who single-handedly invented a genre – the techno-thriller – and became one of the bestselling authors of the 1990s? The Hunt for Red October has it all – fast pacing, great characters, a highly inventive plot that was so realistic it had people wondering if Clancy was privy to some inside information. He also used this book (and all his subsequent ones) to showcase technology at a time when the world was changing so rapidly that it was frightening to think where it might lead. <br /><br />Perhaps most importantly, Clancy gave us an everyman hero that readers could identify with. Jack Ryan isn’t James Bond. Instead, he is someone who uses his intelligence and wits to outthink the opposition. Still, he wasn’t afraid to get his hands dirty, even if that was outside of his comfort zone. That is the great attraction of his character. He could be the guy you have a couple drinks with at the bar before taking in a ballgame. He was one of us in a way the “super spies” never could be. <br /><br />Even though the world has changed a lot since 1984, that identifiable protagonist certainly hasn’t. That’s why <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> rings as true today as it did then. One of the truly great yarns of its time that spawned generations of writers we enjoy to this day. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14167720354774442345">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8746639932641916245">This is a very good story that is incredibly researched. However, in this instance, I'd have to say the movie is better. The reason is that the movie is simplified. This is a very complex book involving military strategy. Even being a ten year veteran of our armed forces, and familiar with military language and acroynms, I found this book slow to read. The author did extensive research into soviet and allied submarines in particular, but also all naval vessels and even aircraft. He receits speci</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8746639932641916245">This is a very good story that is incredibly researched. However, in this instance, I'd have to say the movie is better. The reason is that the movie is simplified. This is a very complex book involving military strategy. Even being a ten year veteran of our armed forces, and familiar with military language and acroynms, I found this book slow to read. The author did extensive research into soviet and allied submarines in particular, but also all naval vessels and even aircraft. He receits specifications frequently throughout the book. It's not out of place or inappropriate, but it's not easy for the average civilian reader to follow at times. The movie simplified this. I choose this Clancy novel to start with as I loved the movie. But after taking two weeks to read this, I'll have to decide if I want to read any others. I'm curious to follow Jack Ryan's career, but doubt I could get through all 12 or 14 books in this series. (Check wikipedia for the list of related books that follow Jack Ryan's career.)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/158637373?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1462364-anila" class="user" title="Anila">Anila</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1462364-anila?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer158637373">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18115330921527497138">Damn, Marko Ramius is an awesome character.<br />Just sayin'.<br /><br /><br />Real review:<br />Well, I've finally read a Clancy book. Yay me?<br />It reminded me a bit of the Honor Harrington series, which I guess makes sense. They're both military, after all; one has spaceships and the other has submarines and other than that the genre conventions seemed about the same. AND THEY BOTH HAVE ONE REALLY ANNOYING HABIT: The 'action action action loooooongwiiiiiinded descriiiiiiption of teeeeechnoooology' format. If I'd been paying a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18115330921527497138">Damn, Marko Ramius is an awesome character.<br />Just sayin'.<br /><br /><br />Real review:<br />Well, I've finally read a Clancy book. Yay me?<br />It reminded me a bit of the Honor Harrington series, which I guess makes sense. They're both military, after all; one has spaceships and the other has submarines and other than that the genre conventions seemed about the same. AND THEY BOTH HAVE ONE REALLY ANNOYING HABIT: The 'action action action loooooongwiiiiiinded descriiiiiiption of teeeeechnoooology' format. If I'd been paying attention instead of trying not to fall asleep in those bits I would have learned more about submarines than I ever wanted to know. As it was, I kinda skipped those bits.<br />Plot-wise, there's a lot of buildup. Like most of the book. And while it's interesting and yes, it's necessary, there are so many threads and they were disconnected for so long that I lost track of them. Clearly, Clancy is not an 'in late out early' sort of writer. Or maybe this is a first book thing?<br />I don't think I'd classify this as a thriller of any sort, because it was never really thrilling. Is it a spoiler to say that of course they got the Red October away safely and no one knew? Frankly, I don't think so. I mean, if they failed there would have been no book and if the Russians had found out Clancy would have had to turn this into a series. Since neither of these things are true, the operations must have been a success. Simple logical deduction. So this isn't a book that you want to read to find out <em>what</em> happened so much as <em>how</em> it happened, and at that Clancy excels. I'm obviously not a submariner, but this has been well-recieved by the navy and certainly seemed meticulously researched.<br /><br />Clancy is now on my radar (ahem, pun?) enough that I'll read more of his work later. I'm in no big rush, though. Also, this book was difficult for me to get through and I don't need another millstone novel to slow me down reading everything else.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18115330921527497138">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_245573257">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245573257" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5685608-john-e-branch-jr" class="left imgcol" title="John E. Branch Jr."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311526969p2/5685608.jpg" alt="John E. Branch Jr." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/245573257?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5685608-john-e-branch-jr" class="user" title="John E. Branch Jr.">John E. Branch Jr.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1001555.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Hardcover 9780870212857" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5685608-john-e-branch-jr?shelf=techno-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">techno-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer245573257">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3245909013670422968">Assuming the Wikipedia entry on the novel to be correct in <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hunt_for_Red_October#Publication_history">an unattributed assertion,</a> Tom Clancy hadn't submitted the manuscript of this book, his first novel, anywhere else before giving the U.S. Naval Institute Press a look at it. He was probably lucky in that, as was the press, for Clancy's novel was different enough from other military thrillers of the time that he quite likely would've received rejections and may have given up. (<a title="J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>, among others, faced the same rejections but per</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3245909013670422968">Assuming the Wikipedia entry on the novel to be correct in <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hunt_for_Red_October#Publication_history">an unattributed assertion,</a> Tom Clancy hadn't submitted the manuscript of this book, his first novel, anywhere else before giving the U.S. Naval Institute Press a look at it. He was probably lucky in that, as was the press, for Clancy's novel was different enough from other military thrillers of the time that he quite likely would've received rejections and may have given up. (<a title="J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>, among others, faced the same rejections but persisted; her first novel, though represented by an agent, was turned down by a dozen more likely British publishers before finding a home at a small house called Bloomsbury, which gave it an initial print run of only 1,000.) When the Naval Institute hardcover of <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> came out, I was working at a small bookstore that had decided to stock a few copies. My father had served on submarines in two wars and had raised me on tales of the "silent service," and I even knew of the Naval Institute, because my father often passed me copies of their <em>Proceedings.</em> So I bought one of those copies, reveled in it, and soon passed it along to my father, who also admired it (or else I bought it for him and he soon lent it back to me).<br /><br />In a way, then, my father and I contributed to creating a monster. This book became a great success in its paperback edition, and Clancy went on to become a brand, a machine, an industry. The later books of his that I've read or looked into have exploited the methods of <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> but lack its relatively sleek efficiency. One of them, <a title="The Sum of All Fears by Tom Clancy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/957388.The_Sum_of_All_Fears">The Sum of All Fears</a>, was more than 500 pages longer than this novel; I tolerated it mainly because it filled a good deal of my time during a depressed period.<br /><br />All of Clancy's books may fulfill a rather fundamental desire. Men and machines and conflict have together been the stuff of some of our stories since the <em>Iliad</em> (yes, mechanisms and weaponry must be counted a feature of that tale too, considering the role played by chariots, swords, and even the shield of Achilles). Clancy lacks a good deal in comparison to Homer, of course: the other realms of life introduced by the <em>Odyssey,</em> for instance, not to mention what some critics since Matthew Arnold have labeled the nobility of Homer's writing. But if Clancy's fictional technique is limited and pretty old-fashioned in most ways, he did develop something notable in <em>Red October,</em> a particular demonstration that our machines are now complex enough that their capabilities and our interactions with them make them akin to genuine characters: they're important instruments in the story, though not yet agents of their own. If even Homer understood that in his way (recall that Patroclus borrowed the armor of Achilles and for a time scared the Trojans with the deception), Clancy deserves credit for bringing the recognition up to date.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3245909013670422968">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a href="/book/show/415020.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425133514" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3634270-evan-mcb?shelf=action-for-dads" class="actionLinkLite">action-for-dads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer219028147">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14087328546382454024">If you ever want to come across really well in an interview with a Navy Officer, be sure to use this book as the answer for "What is the last good book you read?" This will give the interviewing officer a chance to recount the story of how he once met Tom Clancy on a submarine (every Naval Officer has met Tom Clancy on a submarine at least two times). It's not necessary to actually read the book for this, as you can get by with just seeing the movie, UNLESS the officer starts asking you question</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14087328546382454024">If you ever want to come across really well in an interview with a Navy Officer, be sure to use this book as the answer for "What is the last good book you read?" This will give the interviewing officer a chance to recount the story of how he once met Tom Clancy on a submarine (every Naval Officer has met Tom Clancy on a submarine at least two times). It's not necessary to actually read the book for this, as you can get by with just seeing the movie, UNLESS the officer starts asking you questions about which characters are black and which are Scottish, as these are elements that were changed around during the process of adapting "October" to the silver screen. <br /><br />Another rather large element that was changed from book to movie is that when writing the novel, Clancy intended every character (and, indeed, the narrator) to be portrayed by the voice of Alec Baldwin, not just CIA agent Jack Ryan. Fortunately, this is an effect easily replicated in the reader's own mind during reading, especially when there is a dramatic shouting scene, and especially when these dramatic shouts are either "Jesus Christ!" or "Jonesy!"</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14087328546382454024">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_177480544">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177480544" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5649720-rebecca" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1322357734p2/5649720.jpg" alt="Rebecca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/177480544?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5649720-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5649720-rebecca?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer177480544">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2536101520901850811">I've read this a couple times, all when I was significantly younger and more ignorant of Russian history and politics. It was pretty interesting to go back and reread it, both from a hindsight perspective and from the perspective of actually understanding what's going on with the Russian politics.<br /><br />One thing I have to hand to Clancy right off the bat--while I get a lot of nuances I missed in middle school, there's nothing earth-shattering. He did a good enough job explaining things that I got enou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2536101520901850811">I've read this a couple times, all when I was significantly younger and more ignorant of Russian history and politics. It was pretty interesting to go back and reread it, both from a hindsight perspective and from the perspective of actually understanding what's going on with the Russian politics.<br /><br />One thing I have to hand to Clancy right off the bat--while I get a lot of nuances I missed in middle school, there's nothing earth-shattering. He did a good enough job explaining things that I got enough of the gist the first time to follow the story. And when talking about Russian politics, that's quite the accomplishment.<br /><br />This is probably one of the best military thrillers ever written. It's surprisingly short for the genre, and contains very little filler. We bounce between Moscow and Washington, the surface and the bottom of the sea, but it's all necessary to the story. And yet, it's also amazing how many subplots get woven in--a mole in Congress, a mole on the ship, Ryan's budding career, Skip's aborted one. We're introduced to a lot of characters who will play bigger roles in later books, but we get enough of a sense of each right now and no one feels wasted or overdeveloped for the current novel. The pacing is tight, the tension incredibly well drawn out. From what I understand of naval technology and procedure, Clancy's totally on top of his tech.<br /><br />But what's endearing about this book is the character development. Too many thrillers go only for broad caricatures. This one gives us the details that make people feel human. It's the little gestures--the Russian officer who really wants to try an American cigarette but is too proud to ask, the American sonar operator whose college prank went awry, the fact that people can be jerks and still be good officers and people can be enemies and still be good people. It's amazing how many of the little moments had stuck with me even when action sequences didn't.<br /><br />Oh, Ryan is a bit of a Marty Stu (he gets worse in later books). He's a self-made millionaire who just happens to be the brilliantest intelligence officer and also friends with the royal family? Really? But it's pretty much expected of the genre, so I'll give it a pass. And he has flaws, plenty of them. He makes some mistakes. And most importantly, he doesn't single-handedly save the day. Like real warfare, this is a collaborative effort, and we see all the men and women who play a part. And each of them come across as a real human being. It's not just engrossing, it's refreshing. <br /><br />This is now historical instead of current, but it holds up remarkably well. Very few in the genre can say the same. Kudos, Mr. Clancy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2536101520901850811">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62202648?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2384753-karla" class="user" title="Karla">Karla</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62202648">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14184407117570775521">My husband was a submariner and this book rang true from start to finish. We both read this book many years ago, even prior to the movie, and were amazed at the knowledge Clancy had of the US Navy sub force. It is well researched and given the time frame in which it is set, entirely plausible. After living life with the military in a time when you only knew what the Navy thought you had a "need to know", it was relatively easy to imagine that the premise this story is built on could actually hav</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14184407117570775521">My husband was a submariner and this book rang true from start to finish. We both read this book many years ago, even prior to the movie, and were amazed at the knowledge Clancy had of the US Navy sub force. It is well researched and given the time frame in which it is set, entirely plausible. After living life with the military in a time when you only knew what the Navy thought you had a "need to know", it was relatively easy to imagine that the premise this story is built on could actually have happened. Tom Clancy weaves a great page-turner full of intrigue and action and it is a book that is very hard to put down. This was one of his earlier books and is a well-crafted story. Clancy does tremendous research on all of his books, but I do feel his later books are more about information and less about fictional stories. Maybe because it was the first book of his that I read and echoed my personal life, but this is my favorite of his books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14184407117570775521">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer244634824">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5180475799430264934">One of Clancy's earlier books, the good kind that read more richly than the light and profuse fluff of his more recent work. <br />My favorite aspect of the book is the transitioning, which lends itself to heighten the action for certain situations. I also appreciate the detailed tangents that Clancy can go off in to in order to explain a certain topic to the reader. <br />I am not going to summarize the book in great detail. The movie does a good job of that, cutting out interesting side commentary that ad</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5180475799430264934">One of Clancy's earlier books, the good kind that read more richly than the light and profuse fluff of his more recent work. <br />My favorite aspect of the book is the transitioning, which lends itself to heighten the action for certain situations. I also appreciate the detailed tangents that Clancy can go off in to in order to explain a certain topic to the reader. <br />I am not going to summarize the book in great detail. The movie does a good job of that, cutting out interesting side commentary that adds flavor to the story in order to keep the movie to a certain time (by the way, whatever happened to intermissions? I paid $10.50, I want my money's worth!). <br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379751151i/132495.jpg" /><br /><span>[image error]</span><br />For those who don't intend to watch the movie and want a summary, here is the short and sweet: our man Jack Ryan is called back to the US by the CIA to put his skills as an analyst towards figuring out what is so special about a new Soviet submarine, and then eventually where it is going. The thrilling aspect of the book comes in two major pieces: the captain of the Soviet sub heading towards the US with the Soviet navy in tow, and Jack Ryan getting down to figuring out just what is going on. It is not a mystery, just a good cold war thriller. <br />I love Clancy's style and most of his topics, though his dialogue can be generic. It shows that he has spent a lot of time talking to military personnel... <br />Five stars for a great story, even with the sometimes lame speaking.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_289439704">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289439704" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5633117-lynn-hallbrooks" class="left imgcol" title="Lynn Hallbrooks"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1398797959p2/5633117.jpg" alt="Lynn Hallbrooks" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/289439704?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5633117-lynn-hallbrooks" class="user" title="Lynn Hallbrooks">Lynn Hallbrooks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1124906.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425083833" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5633117-lynn-hallbrooks?shelf=my-friend-s-library-books" class="actionLinkLite">my-friend-s-library-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer289439704">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14600269656360831785">This is the second of Tom Clancy’s books that I have read. However, “The Hunt for Red October” was the first book written. I read “Without Remorse” based on my friend’s statement that it was the first book. As it turns out, “Without Remorse” is sort of a Prequel, based on chronological time lines for each book. On the other hand, each book has entirely different story lines and main characters. <br /><br />According to the “About the Author” section, Mr. Clancy’s storyline for “The Hunt for Red October” was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14600269656360831785">This is the second of Tom Clancy’s books that I have read. However, “The Hunt for Red October” was the first book written. I read “Without Remorse” based on my friend’s statement that it was the first book. As it turns out, “Without Remorse” is sort of a Prequel, based on chronological time lines for each book. On the other hand, each book has entirely different story lines and main characters. <br /><br />According to the “About the Author” section, Mr. Clancy’s storyline for “The Hunt for Red October” was inspired by a newspaper article about a mutiny on a Russian frigate. Like many authors, Mr. Clancy did his due diligence on research and combined it with his imagination of what might happen. In his case he did this during times he wasn’t working as an insurance agent. I've read somewhere else that not long after “The Hunt for Red October” book was released; Mr. Clancy was brought to Washington, D.C. for some serious questioning. Having read this book, I can definitely understand why...it is chock full of details. The details while informative, especially if someone had never seen a submarine movie before, were also more than a little distracting to the action at times. Based on the time frame of the book, Cold War era, the main characters’ actions and reactions were quite believable. I know that the character Jack Ryan will occur in future Tom Clancy novels. I will be reading more Tom Clancy to see what happens because I feel certain that the movie version and the books will vary greatly. <br /><br />Mr. Clancy’s love for detail seems to be a pre-dominate theme in both books. I’ve heard from several sources that this is not unusual. So if you haven’t read a Tom Clancy novel and are considering reading one, bare this factor in mind. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14600269656360831785">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_325602927">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325602927" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7672919-jerome" class="left imgcol" title="Jerome"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1330740421p2/7672919.jpg" alt="Jerome" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/325602927?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7672919-jerome" class="user" title="Jerome">Jerome</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19691.The_Hunt_for_Red_October" title="Paperback 9780425172902" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer325602927">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17250522824838194568">Although it was the first of the series to be published, Tom Clancy's The Hunt for Red October is actually the third novel in the Jack Ryan series. It propelled Clancy, who had been an insurance salesman with only a few letters to the editor under his writing belt, to best-selling superstar. His success with military and espionage-related fiction earned him a title he does not readily accept: father of the techno-thriller.<br /><br />This novel, if I remember correctly, was the first work of fiction publish</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17250522824838194568">Although it was the first of the series to be published, Tom Clancy's The Hunt for Red October is actually the third novel in the Jack Ryan series. It propelled Clancy, who had been an insurance salesman with only a few letters to the editor under his writing belt, to best-selling superstar. His success with military and espionage-related fiction earned him a title he does not readily accept: father of the techno-thriller.<br /><br />This novel, if I remember correctly, was the first work of fiction published by the Naval Institute Press, the publishing arm of the United States Naval Institute, a civilian entity which promotes all things naval, including the study of naval history, strategy, technology, and tactics. Some of the Naval Institute Press' other books include A.D. Baker's Fleets of the World, Clay Blair, Jr.'s Silent Victory, and Norman Friedman's Desert Victory: The War for Kuwait. But considering that although Clancy's novel deals with the workings of other federal agencies such as the Central Intelligence Agency, the FBI, the National Security Agency, and both the Executive and Legislative branches, the heart of the story is a sea chase.<br /><br />Based loosely on a 1975 incident in which a Soviet frigate attempted to defect to the West, The Hunt for Red October tells the by-now familiar tale of how Captain First Rank Marko Ramius and a group of selected officers aboard the Soviet Navy's newest Typhoon-class SSBN (the Navy designator for a nuclear-powered ballistic missile submarine, or "boomer") band together to defect to the United States and hand over the Red Navy's most advanced "stealth" submarine.<br /><br />Ramius, you see, is motivated by one of the strongest emotions of all: the desire for revenge against the callous Soviet state. Not only for the death of his wife as a result of negligence by a well-connected surgeon, but for all the injustices he has witnessed from even his early childhood. His father, a Lithuanian communist and devoted Party apparatchik, was responsible for many deaths and unjust acts, and Marko, raised by a decent grandmother, sees both his father and the State as monsters who care for nothing but power and expansion.<br /><br />In this novel, set sometime in the mid-1980s, Clancy introduces us to Jack Ryan, a CIA analyst being groomed by his mentor, Admiral James Greer, for better and more crucial postings within the Agency. Now currently assigned as CIA liaison in London (which puts this novel's setting to be after the current Clancy novel Red Rabbit), it is Ryan who first hands the U.S. its first intelligence data on Red October, courtesy of the British Secret Service.<br /><br />The novel's focus is on Ramius' defection attempt aboard the Red October, which has been modified to use a "caterpillar" drive (described in the movie version as a "jet engine for the water") which enables a sub to glide through the ocean almost undetectably. It also deals with the Red Navy's desperate attempts to seek and destroy the defectors' submarine, and the almost equally desperate moves of an Anglo-American fleet to acquire Red October.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17250522824838194568">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14822783541811663057"> The Hunt for Red October begins with some background behind Marko Ramius. He wants to seek revenge on the Reds for making his life miserable, mainly by killing his beloved wife. His revenge is to take over the Soviet's brand new masterpiece, the Red October, which is a state of the art nuclear submarine with a new propulsion system which makes it nearly invisible to radar. Ramius will lead the Russians on a wild goose chase, and the Americans eventually catch the submarine with some very skille</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14822783541811663057"> The Hunt for Red October begins with some background behind Marko Ramius. He wants to seek revenge on the Reds for making his life miserable, mainly by killing his beloved wife. His revenge is to take over the Soviet's brand new masterpiece, the Red October, which is a state of the art nuclear submarine with a new propulsion system which makes it nearly invisible to radar. Ramius will lead the Russians on a wild goose chase, and the Americans eventually catch the submarine with some very skilled sonarmen and some extremely good luck. In the end, Ramius is welcomed into America, and some other Russian submariners as well. <br /> This book would be great for somebody who loves a thrilling book. However, some of the material may be difficult for some to read, as there is a lot of military talk and the reader will need to know Russian history. Older teenagers and up would love this book. Otherwise it is a book that everybody should read. Tom Clancy made a format that is very gripping, and you won't want to put the book down. The content seems so accurate to detail that it seems that the author may have been writing a biography. </span>
